{"Quotes": "[1] \"On the basis of surface science measurements, density functional calculations, and catalytic reactions under realistic conditions, we describe here a strategy to achieve this goal that takes advantage of the confinement effect at interfaces between nanostructured ferrous oxides (FeO) and metal (Pt) substrates.\"\n\n[2] \"Catalytic reaction experiments on the supported Pt-Fe catalysts prepared by a dedicated and reproducible synthesis method show that the identified ensemble is highly active, selective, and robust for CO oxidation, even under operating conditions of a proton-exchange membrane fuel cell (PEMFC).\"\n\n[3] \"Among various model systems considered, the FeO1-x/Pt(111) surface presents the highest reactivity because of the presence of the CUF sites.\"\n\n[4] \"For the Pt/SiO2 catalysts, CO conversion is negligible below RT, but increases slowly with temperature. At 473 K, only 70% CO was reacted off. In contrast, the Pt-Fe/SiO2 catalysts show a high activity, with almost 100% CO conversion and 100% CO selectivity at RT.\"\n\n[5] \"Depending on the CUF sites, O2 may either dissociate directly to atomic O without barrier, or adsorb molecularly first with a binding energy of about 1.51 eV per O2 (Fig. 2A) and afterward dissociate to atomic O with a barrier of 0.42 eV [the corresponding transition state (TS) shown in Fig. 2B].\"\n\n[6] \"CO oxidation on FeO1-x/Pt(111) might maintain its activity even in the presence of H2 because dissociative adsorption of H2 on Pt suffers from CO poisoning.\"\n\n[7] \"We show that the structural ensemble was highly efficient for carbon monoxide oxidation at low temperature under typical operating conditions of a proton-exchange membrane fuel cell.\"\n\n[8] \"The interface-confined CUF sites together with the metal supports are active for dioxygen activation, producing reactive dissociated oxygen atoms.\"\n\n[9] \"Guided by these insights, we prepared Pt-Fe [4 weight percent (wt %) Pt, 0.5 wt % Fe] nanoparticles (NPs) and Pt (4 wt %) NPs supported on nanosized silica spheres.\"\n\n[10] \"CO PROX reactions under stoichiometric condition (1% CO and 0.5% O2, 98.5% H2, 0.1 M Pa, 36000 ml g1 h1) are conducted on the Pt-Fe/SiO2 and Pt/SiO2 catalysts.\"", "English": "The literature provides significant insights into how Pt-Fe bimetallic catalysts influence the mechanisms and efficiencies of CO oxidation in reactor studies:\n\n1. Mechanism: The catalytic activity is attributed to coordinatively unsaturated ferrous (CUF) sites at the interface between nanostructured ferrous oxides (FeO) and platinum (Pt) substrates. These CUF sites, along with neighboring Pt atoms, are highly active for O2 activation and CO oxidation.\n\n2. Efficiency: Pt-Fe/SiO2 catalysts show significantly higher activity for CO oxidation compared to Pt/SiO2 catalysts. At room temperature, Pt-Fe/SiO2 catalysts achieve almost 100% CO conversion and selectivity, while Pt/SiO2 catalysts show negligible activity.\n\n3. Reaction conditions: The Pt-Fe catalysts maintain high activity, selectivity, and robustness even under operating conditions of a proton-exchange membrane fuel cell (PEMFC). They also show potential for maintaining activity in the presence of H2.\n\n4. O2 activation: Depending on the CUF sites, O2 may either dissociate directly without a barrier or adsorb molecularly before dissociating with a low energy barrier.\n\n5. Preferential oxidation (PROX): The catalysts were also tested for CO PROX reactions in the presence of excess H2, demonstrating their potential for fuel cell applications.\n\nThe study does not directly address water gas shift reactions or methane conversions. {"Quotes": "\"According to the dual pathway mechanism proposed by Breiter and co-workers,911 the intermediate COads generated in the indirect pathway can be strongly adsorbed on the Pt surface, and the reaction active sites on the Pt become occupied, leading to a severe decrease in reaction kinetics.\"\n\n\"In general, the bifunctional mechanism and ligand effect (electronic effect) were proposed to account for the enhancement of the electrocatalytic activity of PtMe catalysts for MOR.\"\n\n\"As for CO oxidation being a structure-sensitive reaction, considerable variables such as crystal face, solution PH, anion adsorption, defects including steps and kinks, pre-history of the electrode, and the size and shape of nanoparticles have all shown important influence on the kinetics of CO oxidation.\"\n\n\"Considerable efforts have been made to obtain highly dispersed RuSex particles with high concentrations of surface sites, thus enhancing the mass activity.\"\n\n\"Regarding the role of Se, Alonso-Vante held that chalcogen additives protected the Ru metal from oxidation.\"\n\n\"Pt alloying with base metals is widely used to enhance the electrocatalytic performance, but contamination of the base metal should be carefully dealt with before practical applications.\"\n\n\"Recently, Jinnouchi et al. showed site-dependent dissolution potentials of Pt particles in which Pt atoms at edges, due to their higher d-band centres, dissolved more easily than Pt atoms on flat surfaces.\"", "English": "The provided literature does not directly address all aspects of the question, particularly regarding water gas shift reaction and methane conversions in reactor studies. However, it offers insights into how Pt-based bimetallic catalysts influence CO oxidation mechanisms and efficiencies:\n\n1. Bimetallic catalysts, especially Pt-based ones, can enhance reaction kinetics through bifunctional mechanisms and electronic effects. The secondary metal (e.g., Ru) can protect the primary metal (Pt) from oxidation and modify its electronic properties.\n\n2. CO oxidation is structure-sensitive, affected by factors such as crystal face, pH, defects, nanoparticle size/shape, and surface site concentration.\n\n3. The addition of a second metal can help activate water dissociation at lower potentials, promoting oxidation of CO adsorbed on Pt sites. It can also alter Pt's electronic properties to weaken CO adsorption.\n\n4. Intermediate species like COads can strongly adsorb on catalyst surfaces, occupying active sites and decreasing reaction kinetics. Bimetallic catalysts can help mitigate this issue.\n\n5. {"Quotes": "[1] \"The PtSnOx system has been studied for many years as it has shown to catalyze the CO oxidation at moderate temperatures (ca. 120 C), where neither platinum nor tin dioxide alone has stable activity. The high activity of PtSnOx system has been ascribed to a synergistic bifunctional mechanism in which Pt provides the adsorption sites for CO, while oxygen adsorbs dissociatively on SnOx\"\n\n[2] \"Schubert et al. have investigated PROX on vulcan supported PtSn catalysts and obtained higher activity and selectivity than commercial Pt/Al2O3 catalyst at low temperatures. Their temperature-programmed desorption (TPD), in situ diffuse reflectance IR Fourier transform spectroscopy, and X-ray photon spectroscopy (XPS) measurements revealed that (i) CO surface coverage on the metallic particles is high and decreases with temperature, (ii) only part of the Sn is reduced, included in PtSn alloy particles, while another part forms SnOx islands beside the active particles.\"\n\n[3] \"Addition of methane to the feed used in SET I. 14 reduced the CO conversion significantly at 135 C from ca. 75% to ca. 50% (Fig. 7a). The chromatographic data showed that there is insignificant methane oxidation at 135 C as well as at other lower temperature levels; thus, the possible explanation for the observed decrease in CO conversion level may be the adsorption competition between CH4 and the CO oxidation reactants.\"\n\n[4] \"Owing to that, the necessity of O-spillover (or transfer) through the support is completely eliminated. Thus, on the basis of our current experimental results and our previous experimental and theoretical findings as well, we can suggest a basic CO oxidation surface mechanism for CO and O2-only feed on Pt3Sn sites involving the following steps:\n\n1 CO (g) → CO·Pt\n2 O2 (g) → O·Sn and/or O2 (g) → O·PtSn\nCO·Pt + O·Sn → CO2 (g) and/or CO·Pt + O·PtSn → CO2·(g)\"\n\n[5] \"PtSn/AC-N catalyst was tested negative for water gas shift reaction activity at 150 C which eliminates the possibility of CO conversion due to WGS at elevated temperatures.\"", "English": "Bimetallic Pt-based catalysts, particularly PtSn systems, significantly influence the mechanisms and efficiencies of CO oxidation, water gas shift reaction, and methane conversions in reactor studies:\n\n1. CO Oxidation: PtSn catalysts show higher activity and selectivity at lower temperatures compared to monometallic Pt catalysts. This is attributed to a synergistic bifunctional mechanism where Pt provides CO adsorption sites while SnOx provides dissociative oxygen adsorption sites. The PtSn system catalyzes CO oxidation at moderate temperatures (around 120°C) where neither Pt nor SnO2 alone shows stable activity.\n\n2. Water Gas Shift Reaction: The PtSn/AC-N catalyst was found to be inactive for the water gas shift reaction at 150°C, eliminating the possibility of CO conversion due to WGS at elevated temperatures.\n\n3. Methane Conversion: The presence of CH4 in the feed reduced CO conversion, likely due to adsorption competition between CH4 and CO oxidation reactants. This suggests that bimetallic catalysts may not necessarily improve methane conversion.\n\n4. Catalyst Structure: In PtSn catalysts, only part of the Sn is reduced and included in PtSn alloy particles, while another part forms SnOx islands beside the active particles. This structure contributes to the catalyst's enhanced performance.\n\n5. Reaction Mechanism: A basic CO oxidation mechanism on Pt3Sn sites is proposed, involving CO adsorption on Pt and O2 adsorption on Sn or PtSn sites, eliminating the need for O-spillover through the support.\n\nFuture UHV studies could provide valuable insights by:\n1. Investigating the surface structure and composition of Pt-based bimetallic catalysts under controlled conditions.\n2. Studying the adsorption and reaction mechanisms of CO, O2, and CH4 on well-defined Pt-Sn surfaces.\n3. Examining the role of SnOx islands and their interaction with Pt in the catalytic process.\n4. Comparing the behavior of model surfaces with supported catalysts to bridge the gap between UHV studies and real catalytic systems.\n\nThese UHV studies could help correlate the findings from reactor studies with model surfaces and supported catalysts, providing a more comprehensive understanding of the catalytic processes and guiding the design of more efficient bimetallic catalysts.", "Chinese": "双金属Pt基催化剂，特别是PtSn系统，显著影响了反应器研究中CO氧化、水煤气变换反应和甲烷转化的机理和效率：\n\n1. CO氧化：PtSn催化剂在较低温度下表现出比单金属Pt催化剂更高的活性和选择性。这归因于协同双功能机制，其中Pt提供CO吸附位点，而SnOx提供解离氧吸附位点。PtSn系统在中等温度（约120°C）下催化CO氧化，而在这个温度下Pt或SnO2单独都不显示稳定活性。\n\n2. 水煤气变换反应：PtSn/AC-N催化剂在150°C下对水煤气变换反应无活性，排除了在高温下由于WGS引起CO转化的可能性。\n\n3. 甲烷转化：CH4存在于进料中会降低CO转化率，这可能是由于CH4与CO氧化反应物之间的吸附竞争。这表明双金属催化剂可能不一定能改善甲烷转化。\n\n4. 催化剂结构：在PtSn催化剂中，只有部分Sn被还原并包含在PtSn合金颗粒中，而另一部分在活性颗粒旁形成SnOx岛。这种结构contributes to催化剂的性能提升。\n\n5. 反应机理：研究提出了Pt3Sn位点上的基本CO氧化机理，涉及CO在Pt上吸附和O2在Sn或PtSn位点上吸附，消除了通过支持物进行O-溢出的需求。\n\n未来的UHV研究可以提供宝贵的见解：\n1. 在受控条件下研究Pt基双金属催化剂的表面结构和组成。\n2. 研究CO、O2和CH4在明确定义的Pt-Sn表面上的吸附和反应机理。\n3. 检查SnOx岛的作用及其与Pt在催化过程中的相互作用。\n4. 比较模型表面与负载型催化剂的行为，以弥合UHV研究与实际催化系统之间的差距。\n\n这些UHV研究可以帮助将反应器研究的发现与模型表面和负载型催化剂相关联，提供对催化过程更全面的理解，并指导设计更高效的双金属催化剂。", "Doi": "10.1016/j.apcatb.2011.06.014"},
{"Quotes": "[1] \"When the bimetallic PtRu/SiO2 catalyst was directly reduced in H2 at 300C, its catalytic behavior was similar to that of monometallic Ru/SiO2 pretreated under similar conditions.\"\n\n[2] \"In contrast, when the same bimetallic catalyst underwent O2/H2 treatment at 300C, a delay of approximately 30C was observed in the CO light-off temperature.\"\n\n[3] \"Such a delay, signifying decreased CO oxidation activity, can be related to a decreased fraction of Ru sites available on the surface of this sample, because the FTIR data suggest that the surface of the metal nanoparticles formed after such treatment is enriched with Pt.\"\n\n[4] \"Given the relatively small fraction of exposed Ru sites, we should also consider that the bimetallic interaction between Pt and Ru may have substantially enhanced the activity of Pt for PROX.\"\n\n[5] \"Such an enhancement can be attributed to the lower strength of CO adsorption, as indicated by the FTIR measurements.\"\n\n[6] \"The FTIR results indicate that the adsorption of CO was substantially weaker on bimetallic samples than on the corresponding monometallic ones.\"\n\n[7] \"Our results indicate that regardless of the pretreatment conditions, the CO adsorbed on the Pt sites of the PtRu/SiO2 samples (band at approximately 2070 cm1) is weakly bound to the surface.\"\n\n[8] \"The results indicate that the presence of Pt stabilizes Ru and prevents its sintering during exposure to oxidizing conditions. {"Quotes": "[1] \"Among the reported heterogeneous catalysts so far for the CO oxidation, PROX reaction and cathodic materials of the PEM fuel cells, supported Pt-Fe nanoparticles prepared by one improved method have been investigated by several groups\"\n\n[2] \"They proposed a so-called bifunctional mechanism and pointed out that the mechanism was clearly different to that of the PROX reaction on Au catalysts supported on TiO2, Al2O3 and ZrO2\"\n\n[3] \"Up to know, a noncompetitive dual site mechanism has been proposed for the PROX reaction over the supported bimetallic Pt-Fe catalyst\"\n\n[4] \"It means that platinum site in Pto state acts as CO adsorption site and iron site in FeOx or Feo state as an O2 dissociative-adsorption site enhances the surface reaction between the reactants on the neighboring sites.\"\n\n[5] \"Very recently, Siani et al. reported the silica-supported Pt, PtFe2 and Pt5Fe2 catalysts prepared from PtFe2(COD)(CO)8 (COD = 1,5-cyclooctadiene) and Pt5Fe2(COD)2(CO)12 organometallic cluster precursors, respectively\"\n\n[6] \"The cluster-derived PtFe/SiO2 catalyst showed improved CO oxidation activity in the presence and absence of hydrogen as compared to that prepared by the conventional methods.\"", "English": "Bimetallic Pt-based catalysts, particularly Pt-Fe systems, significantly influence CO oxidation and related reactions through several mechanisms:\n\n1. Bifunctional mechanism: In Pt-Fe catalysts, Pt sites act as CO adsorption sites while Fe sites serve as O2 dissociative-adsorption sites. This synergistic effect enhances surface reactions between reactants on neighboring sites.\n\n2. Noncompetitive dual site mechanism: This has been proposed for the preferential oxidation (PROX) reaction over supported bimetallic Pt-Fe catalysts.\n\n3. Improved activity: Pt-Fe catalysts, especially those derived from organometallic cluster precursors, have shown enhanced CO oxidation activity compared to conventionally prepared catalysts, both in the presence and absence of hydrogen.\n\n4. Distinct mechanism: The mechanism for Pt-Fe catalysts differs from that of Au catalysts supported on TiO2, Al2O3, and ZrO2.\n\nWhile the literature doesn't directly address water gas shift reactions or methane conversions, the principles of bifunctional catalysis may apply to these reactions as well, potentially improving their efficiencies.\n\nRegarding future UHV studies, they could provide valuable insights by:\n1. Examining model surfaces that more closely mimic the structure of supported nanoparticle catalysts.\n2. Investigating atomic-scale interactions between Pt and secondary metals on surfaces.\n3. Correlating surface structure and composition with reactivity for specific reactions.\n4. Studying the dynamics of reactant adsorption and product desorption on bimetallic surfaces.\n\nHowever, current limitations in UHV studies on Pt-based bimetallic surfaces make direct comparisons to real catalysts challenging. These may include difficulties in creating well-defined bimetallic surfaces that accurately represent real catalysts, and challenges in replicating high-pressure, high-temperature conditions of real reactors in UHV environments. Overcoming these limitations could provide a more comprehensive understanding of the catalytic mechanisms at play in these important reactions.", "Chinese": "双金属Pt基催化剂，特别是Pt-Fe系统，通过几种机制显著影响CO氧化和相关反应：\n\n1. 双功能机制：在Pt-Fe催化剂中，Pt位点作为CO吸附位点，而Fe位点作为O2解离吸附位点。这种协同效应增强了相邻位点上反应物之间的表面反应。\n\n2. 非竞争性双位点机制：这种机制被提出用于解释支撑的双金属Pt-Fe催化剂上的优先氧化（PROX）反应。\n\n3. 改进的活性：Pt-Fe催化剂，特别是那些从有机金属簇前体衍生的催化剂，在有氢和无氢条件下都表现出比传统制备方法更好的CO氧化活性。\n\n4. 独特的机制：Pt-Fe催化剂的机制与支撑在TiO2、Al2O3和ZrO2上的Au催化剂的机制不同。\n\n虽然文献没有直接提到水煤气变换反应或甲烷转化，但双功能催化的原理可能也适用于这些反应，潜在地提高它们的效率。\n\n关于未来的UHV研究，它们可能通过以下方式提供宝贵的见解：\n1. 研究更接近支撑纳米粒子催化剂结构的模型表面。\n2. 研究表面上Pt和次要金属之间的原子尺度相互作用。\n3. 将表面结构和成分与特定反应的反应性相关联。\n4. 研究反应物在双金属表面上的吸附和产物脱附动力学。\n\n然而，目前在Pt基双金属表面的UHV研究上存在局限性，使得与实际催化剂的直接比较具有挑战性。这些可能包括难以创建能准确代表真实催化剂的良好定义的双金属表面，以及在UHV环境中复制真实反应器的高压、高温条件的挑战。克服这些限制可以为这些重要反应中的催化机理提供更全面的理解。", "Doi": "10.1007/s10562-008-9513-6"},
{"Quotes": "[1] \"Pt-based intermetallic compounds (IMCs) supported on silica were studied as a catalyst for the preferential oxidation (PROX) of CO in excess hydrogen to obtain the active catalyst at low temperatures.\"\n\n[2] \"Pt3Co/SiO2 and PtCu/SiO2 were more active than Pt/SiO2 and Pt/Al2O3 in the temperature range of 373453 K.\"\n\n[3] \"Infrared (IR), X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS), and adsorption measurements revealed a significant electron transfer from Pt atoms to Co or Cu atoms. The electron-deficient Pt atoms adsorbed CO weakly compared with Pt metal, accelerating the adsorption of oxygen on the IMC surface.\"\n\n[4] \"Kinetic studies indicated that Co and Cu atoms in IMCs also adsorb oxygen. This improved oxygen adsorption likely resulted in the high PROX activity at low temperatures.\"\n\n[5] \"The reaction proceeded through the LangmuirHinshelwood mechanism, as has been proposed on PtFe/mordenite\"\n\n[6] \"On PtCu/SiO2, however, CO conversion increased by 30% with the addition of hydrogen and even further by the addition of water. The enhancing effect of hydrogen reflected the contribution of water produced by the oxidation of hydrogen during the PROX reaction.\"\n\n[7] \"The CO molecules on Pt would be oxidized by oxygen atoms activated on Co, resulting in higher activity of Pt3Co compared with Pt metal.\"", "English": "Pt-based bimetallic catalysts, particularly intermetallic compounds (IMCs) like Pt3Co and PtCu, significantly influence CO oxidation mechanisms and efficiencies in reactor studies. These catalysts show higher activity than pure Pt catalysts at lower temperatures (373-453 K) for preferential oxidation (PROX) of CO in excess hydrogen.\n\nThe enhanced performance of these bimetallic catalysts is attributed to several factors:\n\n1. Electronic effects: Electron transfer from Pt to Co or Cu atoms results in electron-deficient Pt atoms that adsorb CO more weakly than pure Pt, facilitating oxygen adsorption.\n\n2. Improved oxygen adsorption: Co and Cu atoms in the IMCs also adsorb oxygen, contributing to higher PROX activity at low temperatures.\n\n3. Reaction mechanism: The reaction proceeds through a Langmuir-Hinshelwood mechanism, differing from the Rideal mechanism observed on pure Pt surfaces.\n\n4. Synergistic effects: On Pt3Co, CO adsorbed on Pt is oxidized by oxygen atoms activated on Co sites, resulting in higher activity compared to pure Pt.\n\n5. Hydrogen and water effects: For PtCu catalysts, the presence of hydrogen and water significantly enhances CO conversion. The addition of hydrogen increases CO conversion by 30%, with further enhancement by water addition. This effect is attributed to the water produced during the PROX reaction.\n\nThe study does not provide direct information on water gas shift reactions or methane conversions for these bimetallic catalysts. \n\nFuture UHV studies could potentially provide valuable insights by:\n\n1. Investigating the surface structure and composition of well-defined bimetallic surfaces under reaction conditions.\n2. Studying the adsorption and reaction of CO, oxygen, and hydrogen on these surfaces at a molecular level.\n3. Examining the effects of water on the surface chemistry of these bimetallic catalysts.\n4. Comparing the reactivity of model surfaces with supported catalysts to understand the role of the support and particle size effects.\n\nSuch UHV studies could bridge the gap between reactor studies and model surfaces, providing atomic-level insights into the mechanisms underlying the enhanced performance of bimetallic catalysts. This could potentially lead to the design of more efficient catalysts for CO oxidation and related reactions.", "Chinese": "基于铂的双金属催化剂，特别是Pt3Co和PtCu等金属间化合物（IMCs），在反应器研究中显著影响CO氧化机理和效率。这些催化剂在较低温度下（373-453 K）对过量氢气中CO的优先氧化（PROX）表现出比纯Pt催化剂更高的活性。\n\n这些双金属催化剂的增强性能归因于几个因素：\n\n1. 电子效应：Pt向Co或Cu原子的电子转移导致Pt原子缺电子，与纯Pt相比更弱地吸附CO，从而促进氧气吸附。\n\n2. 改善的氧气吸附：IMCs中的Co和Cu原子也吸附氧气，有助于在低温下提高PROX活性。\n\n3. 反应机理：反应通过Langmuir-Hinshelwood机理进行，与纯Pt表面上观察到的Rideal机理不同。\n\n4. 协同效应：在Pt3Co上，吸附在Pt上的CO被在Co位点上活化的氧原子氧化，导致比纯Pt更高的活性。\n\n5. 氢气和水的效应：对于PtCu催化剂，氢气和水的存在显著增强了CO转化。添加氢气使CO转化率增加30%，添加水进一步增强了这一效果。这种效应归因于PROX反应过程中产生的水。\n\n该研究没有直接提供这些双金属催化剂在水煤气变换反应或甲烷转化方面的信息。\n\n未来的超高真空（UHV）研究可能通过以下方式提供有价值的见解：\n\n1. 研究反应条件下定义明确的双金属表面的表面结构和组成。\n2. 在分子水平上研究CO、氧气和氢气在这些表面上的吸附和反应。\n3. 检查水对这些双金属催化剂表面化学的影响。\n4. 比较模型表面与负载型催化剂的反应活性，以了解载体和粒子尺寸效应的作用。\n\n这些UHV研究可以弥合反应器研究与模型表面之间的差距，提供对双金属催化剂增强性能背后机理的原子水平见解。这可能导致设计出更高效的CO氧化和相关反应的催化剂。", "Doi": "10.1016/j.jcat.2008.06.030"},

{"Quotes": "\"The key for the improvement of the CO oxidation rate is to allow for a non-competitive dual-site mechanism for CO and O2. New catalyst formulations are being developed towards supplying these catalysts with an additional site for oxygen adsorption, which will enhance the reaction rate, by addition of a promoter\"\n\n\"An example of this development is the addition of Fe as a promoter for Pt catalysts. The Pt serves as the site for CO adsorption, whereas the Fe oxide promoter dissociates the O2 molecule, resulting in a non-competitive, dual-site mechanism.\"\n\n\"MnOx is reported as high oxygen storage capacity compound. MnOx has been studied in oxidation reactions and as support for Au catalyst in the PROX reaction. MnOx-doped Pt catalysts have been studied for automotive pollution control and for CO oxidation (in H2-free streams).\"\n\n\"Comparing the PROX behavior of all catalysts in Fig. 5(a), we can see that those with a higher content in MnOx (P1M8ASI and P1M15ASI) are more active than Pt/Al2O3, with the following order of activity: P1M15ASI > P1M8ASI > P1A > P1M2ASI > M2P1ASI ≈ P1M2ACI ≈ M2A.\"\n\n\"While the WGS reaction is beneficial in its forward direction, methanation reactions are always detrimental and should be avoided.\"", "English": "Bimetallic catalysts, particularly Pt-based ones, significantly influence CO oxidation mechanisms and efficiencies through a non-competitive dual-site mechanism. {"Quotes": "[1] \"The addition of Re to Pt/Ce0.46Zr0.54O2 was shown to enhance the watergas shift (WGS) rate compared with the rate observed with Pt alone supported on either Ce0.46Zr0.54O2 or Ce0.6Zr0.4O2 at similar Pt weight loadings.\"\n\n[2] \"The results from CO chemisorption showed that the Pt was more highly dispersed on Pt-Re/Ce0.46Zr0.54O2 than on the Pt/Ce0.46Zr0.54O2 or Pt/Ce0.6Zr0.4O2.\"\n\n[3] \"The WGS rate was observed to be proportional to the exposed Pt surface area for the Pt-Re and Pt catalysts; however, the rate per m2 of exposed Pt for Pt-Re/ Ce0.46Zr0.54O2 was higher than that of Pt/Ce0.46Zr0.54O2 or Pt/Ce0.6Zr0.4O2.\"\n\n[4] \"The difference in the rates upon the addition of Re to Pt WGS catalysts suggests that the role of Re in enhancing the WGS activity of Pt is more complex than to just increase the Pt dispersion.\"\n\n[5] \"If the only function of Re was to increase the Pt dispersion, one would expect the same WGS activity for both Pt and Pt-Re catalysts.\"\n\n[6] \"A bifunctional redox mechanism is used to explain this synergism. In this mechanism, CO is adsorbed on the platinum, then oxygen is transferred from the ceria to the platinum, where the CO is oxidized (CO2) and the ceria is reduced (Ce4+  Ce3+); finally, the reduced ceria is reoxidized (Ce3+  Ce4+) by the dissociative adsorption of H2O, releasing H2 in the process.\"", "English": "Bimetallic catalysts, particularly Pt-based ones like Pt-Re, significantly influence the mechanisms and efficiencies of the water gas shift (WGS) reaction in reactor studies. The addition of Re to Pt/Ce0.46Zr0.54O2 enhances the WGS rate compared to Pt alone on similar supports. This enhancement is partly due to increased Pt dispersion, as shown by CO chemisorption studies. However, the effect goes beyond just improved dispersion, as the rate per unit of exposed Pt surface area is higher for Pt-Re catalysts than for Pt alone.\n\nThe mechanism for the WGS reaction on these catalysts is believed to be a bifunctional redox mechanism, where CO adsorbs on Pt, oxygen transfers from the ceria support to Pt for CO oxidation, and the reduced ceria is then reoxidized by water, releasing hydrogen.\n\nThe synergistic effect between Pt and Re suggests possible electronic or structural modifications that affect the catalytic properties. The role of Re in enhancing the WGS activity of Pt is more complex than simply increasing Pt dispersion.\n\nCurrent reactor studies provide valuable insights into the performance of these bimetallic catalysts, but they have limitations in elucidating the precise nature of the active sites and reaction mechanisms at the atomic scale. {"Quotes": "[1] \"The catalyst is 0.5% Ru and 0.5% Pt (w/w) supported on mixture of alumina, ceria and zirconia (75/4.4/20.6%, w/w), washcoated on a ceramic monolith.\"\n\n[2] \"We already studied the activity of this 0.5/0.5% Pt/Ru catalyst for partial oxidation, speculating that combustion and reforming of methane occurs sequentially, and that is clearly identified also by tests on the global reaction, without studying each single reaction in the mechanism.\"\n\n[3] \"Through specific tests with selected mixtures, we proved that the PtRu catalyst supports the indirect combustion and reforming mechanism in CPO, as already suggested in a previous work.\"\n\n[4] \"The catalyst was active in catalysing all the candidate reactions (steam reforming, dry reforming and direct/reverse water-gas shift).\"\n\n[5] \"Both the direct and the reverse water-gas shift reactions are very fast and not affected by the gas space velocity. They approach the thermodynamic equilibrium, with the direct reaction being more relevant for the global mechanism at low temperature, while the reverse reaction becomes more important at high temperature.\"\n\n[6] \"The steam reforming tests showed that this reaction gives a considerable contribution mainly at the lowest GHSV, explaining the differences in the conversions detected during CPO tests.\"\n\n[7] \"Results indicate that the PtRu catalyst is active also for dry reforming, significantly converting both CO2 and CH4 to H2 and CO.\"", "English": "The bimetallic PtRu catalyst studied in this work influences the mechanisms and efficiencies of CO oxidation, water gas shift reaction, and methane conversions in several ways:\n\n1. It supports an indirect combustion and reforming mechanism for catalytic partial oxidation (CPO) of methane, where complete combustion occurs first, followed by reforming reactions.\n\n2. The catalyst is active for multiple reactions involved in methane conversion, including steam reforming, dry reforming, and both direct and reverse water-gas shift reactions.\n\n3. For the water-gas shift reaction, both forward and reverse reactions proceed very quickly on the PtRu catalyst, approaching thermodynamic equilibrium and not being significantly affected by gas space velocity. The direct reaction is more relevant at low temperatures, while the reverse reaction becomes more important at high temperatures.\n\n4. In steam reforming, the catalyst's activity is more pronounced at lower gas hourly space velocities (GHSV), which explains differences in methane conversion observed during CPO tests.\n\n5. The catalyst is also active for dry reforming, converting both CO2 and CH4 to H2 and CO.\n\n6. The bimetallic nature of the catalyst, combining Pt and Ru, likely contributes to its effectiveness across multiple reaction pathways, with Ru probably playing a crucial role in promoting reforming reactions.\n\nFuture UHV studies could potentially provide insights by:\n\n1. Investigating the surface chemistry and adsorption properties of Pt-Ru alloys to understand how the bimetallic nature influences reactivity.\n\n2. Examining the oxidation state and distribution of Pt and Ru atoms on model surfaces to correlate with catalyst performance.\n\n3. Studying the interaction of reaction intermediates with Pt-Ru surfaces to elucidate reaction mechanisms at the molecular level.\n\n4. Comparing results from model Pt-Ru surfaces with supported catalysts to bridge the gap between idealized and real catalytic systems.\n\nHowever, UHV studies on Pt-based bimetallic surfaces can be challenging due to the complexity of alloy surfaces and the difficulty in preparing well-defined bimetallic model systems. Overcoming these limitations could provide crucial insights into the fundamental principles governing the catalytic behavior observed in reactor studies.", "Chinese": "本研究中所研究的双金属PtRu催化剂通过以下几种方式影响CO氧化、水煤气变换反应和甲烷转化的机理和效率：\n\n1. 它支持甲烷催化部分氧化（CPO）的间接燃烧和重整机制，其中先发生完全燃烧，然后进行重整反应。\n\n2. 该催化剂对甲烷转化涉及的多种反应都具有活性，包括蒸汽重整、干重整以及正向和逆向水煤气变换反应。\n\n3. 对于水煤气变换反应，PtRu催化剂使正向和逆向反应都能非常快速地进行，接近热力学平衡，且不受气体空速的显著影响。在低温下正向反应更为相关，而在高温下逆向反应变得更重要。\n\n4. 在蒸汽重整中，催化剂的活性在较低的气体小时空速（GHSV）下更为显著，这解释了CPO测试中观察到的甲烷转化差异。\n\n5. 该催化剂对干重整也有活性，将CO2和CH4转化为H2和CO。\n\n6. 催化剂的双金属性质，即Pt和Ru的结合，可能是其在多种反应途径中都有效的原因，其中Ru可能在促进重整反应中起着关键作用。\n\n未来的超高真空（UHV）研究可能提供以下洞见：\n\n1. 研究Pt-Ru合金的表面化学和吸附特性，以了解双金属性质如何影响反应活性。\n\n2. 检查模型表面上Pt和Ru原子的氧化态和分布，以与催化剂性能相关联。\n\n3. 研究反应中间体与Pt-Ru表面的相互作用，以阐明分子水平的反应机理。\n\n4. 比较模型Pt-Ru表面与负载型催化剂的结果，以弥合理想化和实际催化系统之间的差距。\n\n然而，由于合金表面的复杂性和制备明确定义的双金属模型系统的困难，对基于Pt的双金属表面进行UHV研究可能具有挑战性。克服这些限制可能会为反应器研究中观察到的催化行为的基本原理提供关键见解。", "Doi": "10.1016/j.apcata.2009.12.021"},
{"Quotes": "[1] \"The catalytic data reported here show that the monometallic 0.4Pt/Al2O3 catalyst is slightly more active than the 4Ni/Al2O3 catalyst in the dry reforming of methane, in spite of the smaller metal content, in agreement with the intrinsically higher activity of platinum with respect to nickel in the reaction.\"\n\n[2] \"However, an improvement in the catalyst activity can be obtained not only by introducing a small amount of Pt on the Ni/Al2O3 catalyst (0.04Pt4Ni/Al2O3 catalyst) but also adding a significant amount of Ni to the Pt/Al2O3 catalyst (0.4Pt4Ni/Al2O3 catalyst).\"\n\n[3] \"It is evident that some kind of synergy occurs between Ni and Pt on the alumina carrier, improving DRM activity, in terms of conversion. {"Quotes": "[1] \"The combined effect of Ni and Pt can produce a coke-resistant catalyst.\"\n\n[2] \"The results demonstrated that the bimetallic NiPt/zeolite catalyst showed lower activity (e.g., NiPtY and NiPtβ activities were 1.70 and 1.90 gmetal1 h1, respectively) than that of the monometallic Pt/zeolite catalyst (e.g., PtY and Ptβ activities were close to 2.0 and 3.20 gmetal1 h1, respectively).\"\n\n[3] \"The behaviour of NiPt bimetallic samples is quite similar to that of Ptβ; in others words, NiPtY and NiPtβ produce a large amount of graphite-like carbon and a small amount of filamentous carbon.\"\n\n[4] \"The activity of bimetallic catalysts can also be explained by the fact that the presence of a second metal such as platinum exposes the nickel to the reactants, meaning a redispersion of Ni occurs due to the addition/dispersion of a second metal, e.g., platinum\"\n\n[5] \"In addition, in the case of NiPt bimetallic systems, the rate of decomposition of methane is slower than that on monometallic nickel systems. First, methane cracking and Boudouard reactions (reactions (VIII) and (XIX)) produce surface carbon on the Ni particles embedded in the support. Second, the diffusion of carbon through the Ni particles occurs, followed by segregation at the rear. {"Quotes": "[1] \"A series of PtNi bimetallic catalysts supported on δ-Al2O3 to be used in carbon dioxide reforming of methane was prepared and tested with the objective of optimizing the Ni/Pt metal composition to obtain high activity and stability.\"\n\n[2] \"The activity results showed that the catalytic performance of bimetallic PtNi samples strongly depended on the metal loadings and Ni/Pt loading ratio.\"\n\n[3] \"Among all the catalysts, 0.3%Pt10%Ni/Al2O3, which has the lowest Ni/Pt ratio, exhibited the highest catalytic activity and stability.\"\n\n[4] \"The combined characterization and catalyst performance tests results reveal that low Ni/Pt molar loading ratio of 0.3%Pt10%Ni/Al2O3 sample led to a relatively easy reduction of nickel oxide species and smaller nano-sized nickel particles having better dispersion caused by the intimate interaction between Pt and Ni sites in the closed vicinity.\"\n\n[5] \"The results of the combined dry reforming and partial oxidation tests strongly indicated a change in surface reaction mechanism depending on the Pt load and Ni/Pt ratio of the catalysts.\"\n\n[6] \"The changes in the catalysts activity and stability under the presence of an additional oxygen source were determined through addition of small amounts of either oxygen or water vapor to the feed stream.\"", "English": "The literature primarily focuses on PtNi bimetallic catalysts for carbon dioxide reforming of methane, providing insights into how these catalysts influence reaction mechanisms and efficiencies in reactor studies. {"Quotes": "[1] \"Among a number of catalysts reported to be active for PROX, supported platinum catalysts have been considered to be promising in view of their high catalytic performance.\"\n\n[2] \"PtCo bimetallic catalyst supported on yttria-stabilized zirconia (YSZ) is highly efficient for PROX in a H2-rich gas stream even with a small amount of Pt (0.5wt%) at temperatures below 423K.\"\n\n[3] \"The presence of isolated bimetallic PtCo nanoparticles interacting with the support seems to give rise to this high catalytic activity.\"\n\n[4] \"For CO oxidation, it has been proposed that the lattice oxygen and interfacial metalsupport interaction play a crucial role in promoting CO oxidation when metal species are supported on an oxygen-ion-conducting support.\"\n\n[5] \"Temperature-programmed reduction (TPR) was conducted to try to determine the interactions between Pt and Co, as well as those between Pt, Co oxides (CoOx), and YSZ\"\n\n[6] \"Three main reactions take place in this system. The reaction that competes most effectively with CO oxidation [Eq.(1)] is H2 oxidation [Eq.(2)] because of the H2-rich conditions in the gas stream in practical fuel cell applications. In addition, CO can consume additional H2 by undergoing hydrogenation [Eq.(3)], a process also known as methanation, which should be avoided unless the CO concentration in the reactant stream is quite low, because it consumes relatively large amounts of hydrogen (3mol per mol CO).\"", "English": "Bimetallic catalysts, particularly Pt-based ones like PtCo, significantly influence the mechanisms and efficiencies of CO oxidation, water gas shift reaction, and methane conversions in reactor studies. PtCo bimetallic catalysts supported on yttria-stabilized zirconia (YSZ) demonstrate high efficiency for preferential CO oxidation (PROX) in hydrogen-rich streams, even with low Pt content (0.5wt%) at temperatures below 423K.\n\nThe enhanced catalytic activity is attributed to the presence of isolated bimetallic PtCo nanoparticles interacting with the support. For CO oxidation, lattice oxygen and interfacial metal-support interactions play crucial roles when metal species are supported on oxygen-ion-conducting supports like YSZ.\n\nThe study used temperature-programmed reduction (TPR) to investigate the interactions between Pt, Co, and the YSZ support, providing insights into the formation and behavior of the bimetallic phase. This technique revealed the presence of new bimetallic PtCo oxides and their reduction at lower temperatures compared to monometallic catalysts.\n\nIn the catalytic system, three main reactions occur: CO oxidation, H2 oxidation, and CO hydrogenation (methanation). H2 oxidation competes most effectively with CO oxidation due to H2-rich conditions in practical fuel cell applications. Methanation should be avoided unless CO concentration is low, as it consumes large amounts of hydrogen.\n\nWhile this research provides valuable insights from reactor studies, it does not directly address UHV studies on Pt-based bimetallic surfaces. Future UHV studies could potentially offer more detailed information on atomic-scale interactions and surface chemistry, helping to correlate findings from reactor studies with model surfaces and supported catalysts. However, UHV studies face limitations in replicating complex catalytic environments, particularly in terms of pressure and the presence of support materials. Bridging the gap between UHV studies and real catalytic conditions remains a challenge in correlating findings with model surfaces and supported catalysts.", "Chinese": "双金属催化剂，特别是以Pt为基础的催化剂（如PtCo），在反应器研究中显著影响了CO氧化、水煤气变换反应和甲烷转化的机理和效率。以氧化钇稳定的氧化锆（YSZ）为载体的PtCo双金属催化剂在富氢气流中对优先CO氧化（PROX）表现出高效性，即使在低Pt含量（0.5wt%）和423K以下的温度下也是如此。\n\n增强的催化活性归因于与载体相互作用的孤立双金属PtCo纳米粒子的存在。对于CO氧化，当金属物种被负载在氧离子导电载体（如YSZ）上时，晶格氧和金属-载体界面相互作用起着至关重要的作用。\n\n研究使用温度程序还原（TPR）技术来研究Pt、Co和YSZ载体之间的相互作用，从而深入了解双金属相的形成和行为。这种技术揭示了新的双金属PtCo氧化物的存在，以及它们相比单金属催化剂在更低温度下的还原过程。\n\n在催化系统中，主要发生三种反应：CO氧化、H2氧化和CO加氢（甲烷化）。由于实际燃料电池应用中富氢条件的存在，H2氧化最有效地与CO氧化竞争。除非CO浓度较低，否则应避免甲烷化，因为它消耗大量氢气。\n\n虽然这项研究提供了反应器研究的宝贵见解，但它并未直接涉及Pt基双金属表面的超高真空（UHV）研究。未来的UHV研究可能会提供原子尺度相互作用和表面化学的更详细信息，有助于将反应器研究的发现与模型表面和负载催化剂相关联。然而，UHV研究在复制复杂的催化环境方面面临局限性，特别是在压力和载体材料存在的方面。弥合UHV研究与实际催化条件之间的差距仍然是将研究结果与模型表面和负载催化剂相关联的一个挑战。", "Doi": "10.1002/anie.200603144"},

{"Quotes": "[1] \"The modification of Ni with Pt suppressed the oxidation of Ni species near the bed inlet in the oxidative steam reforming of methane at 1123 K, although the species on the monometallic Ni catalysts were oxidized under similar conditions.\"\n\n[2] \"This can be due to the decreased oxidation rate of the species and the increased reduction rate caused by the surface modification of Ni with Pt.\"\n\n[3] \"Consequently, the PtNi species can be maintained in the metallic state near the bed inlet, and the species can be the active site for the reforming reaction as well as the combustion reaction, which this leads to a lower bed temperature and smaller temperature gradient than those seen for the monometallic Ni catalysts.\"\n\n[4] \"The additive effect of Pt by the sequential impregnation method (Pt/Ni) was much more significant than that by the co-impregnation method (Pt + Ni) in terms of catalytic performance and catalyst bed temperature profile.\"\n\n[5] \"The combination of EXAFS and FTIR results suggests segregation of Pt atoms on the surface of the PtNi alloy particles.\"\n\n[6] \"Characterization results by means of TEM, TPR, EXAFS, and FTIR suggest that the Pt atoms on the Pt/Ni catalysts were located more preferably on the surface to form a PtNi alloy than those on the Pt + Ni catalysts.\"", "English": "Bimetallic Pt-Ni catalysts significantly influence the mechanisms and efficiencies of methane conversion in reactor studies, particularly in oxidative steam reforming of methane. Key findings include:\n\n1. Pt modification suppresses Ni oxidation near the reactor bed inlet, allowing PtNi species to remain in a metallic state.\n2. This is due to decreased oxidation rates and increased reduction rates caused by Pt surface modification.\n3. PtNi species act as active sites for both reforming and combustion reactions, leading to lower bed temperatures and smaller temperature gradients compared to monometallic Ni catalysts.\n4. The preparation method of bimetallic catalysts is crucial: sequential impregnation (Pt/Ni) is more effective than co-impregnation (Pt+Ni) in terms of catalytic performance and temperature profile control.\n5. Pt atoms preferentially segregate on the surface of PtNi alloy particles, forming a more effective catalyst.\n\nWhile the literature doesn't directly address CO oxidation or water gas shift reactions, the improved oxidation resistance and enhanced reducibility of PtNi catalysts likely benefit these reactions as well.\n\nFuture UHV studies could provide valuable insights by:\n1. Investigating surface structure and composition of model PtNi alloy surfaces under various conditions.\n2. Studying adsorption and reaction mechanisms of relevant species (CH4, H2O, O2, CO) on these model surfaces.\n3. Examining oxidation and reduction kinetics of PtNi surfaces at the atomic scale.\n4. Correlating UHV findings with reactor studies to bridge the pressure and materials gaps between model and real catalysts.\n\nHowever, current UHV studies on Pt-based bimetallic surfaces have limitations in fully replicating the complex conditions of practical catalytic reactors. Bridging this gap between UHV studies and real catalytic systems remains a challenge and an area for future research.", "Chinese": "双金属Pt-Ni催化剂显著影响了反应器研究中甲烷转化的机理和效率，特别是在甲烷的氧化蒸汽重整过程中。主要发现包括：\n\n1. Pt改性抑制了反应器床层入口附近Ni的氧化，使PtNi物种保持金属态。\n2. 这是由于Pt表面修饰导致氧化速率降低和还原速率提高。\n3. PtNi物种既是重整反应又是燃烧反应的活性位点，导致床层温度较低，温度梯度比单金属Ni催化剂小。\n4. 双金属催化剂的制备方法至关重要：顺序浸渍法(Pt/Ni)在催化性能和温度分布控制方面比共浸渍法(Pt+Ni)更有效。\n5. Pt原子优先在PtNi合金颗粒表面偏析，形成更有效的催化剂。\n\n虽然文献没有直接涉及CO氧化或水气变换反应，但PtNi催化剂改善的抗氧化性和增强的还原性可能也有利于这些反应。\n\n未来的UHV研究可以通过以下方式提供有价值的见解：\n1. 研究不同条件下PtNi合金表面的模型表面结构和成分。\n2. 研究相关物种（CH4、H2O、O2、CO）在这些模型表面上的吸附和反应机理。\n3. 在原子尺度上研究PtNi表面的氧化和还原动力学。\n4. 将UHV研究结果与反应器研究相关联，以弥合模型催化剂和实际催化剂之间的压力和材料差距。\n\n然而，目前对Pt基双金属表面的UHV研究在完全复制实际催化反应器的复杂条件方面存在局限性。弥合UHV研究和实际催化系统之间的差距仍然是一个挑战，也是未来研究的一个领域。", "Doi": "10.1016/j.jcat.2006.10.004"},

{"Quotes": "[1] \"Many studies have been made on the approach of combinatorial catalysis especially Pt and Pd for CO oxidation reaction [10]. Using bimetallic system is an attractive alternative that appears to enhance some properties of the catalyst or some synergistic effect as electronic effect/geometry effect.\"\n\n[2] \"Although it is still not yet well understood, it has been established that the bimetallic system improves both activity and selectivity of a great number of reactions [11,12].\"\n\n[3] \"Narui et al. [17] attributed the superior combustion activity of PdPt to higher dispersion of supported particles and suppression of particle growth.\"\n\n[4] \"The catalytic activity was obviously increased with the increasing content of Pd. However, the results at a ratio of Pt: Pd = 1: 9 evidenced that it was not necessary to load Pd in very high loadings. The catalyst with a ratio of Pt: Pd = 1: 7 showed the best performance, 76% CO conversion and 55% selectivity and at 90.110 C.\"\n\n[5] \"When increasing the O2 concentration to twice the stoichiometric ratio of the oxygen concentration (1% O2 ), the CO conversion increased to 76% at 90.110 C. Ninty nine percent CO conversion of 1% CO at 90 C can be achieved by increasing the oxygen concentration to 2%.\"\n\n[6] \"An enhancement of CO oxidation reaction can be apparently observed when adding 10% water vapor in the feed. At 90 C, when there was no water vapor in the feed stream the CO conversion was about 76% and when adding 10% water vapor in the feed stream the CO conversion was increased to 85%.\"\n\n[7] \"The CO conversion substantially dropped from 76% to 50% at 90.110 C when increasing CO2 concentration in the feed stream. The presence of CO2 also affected the selectivity in the temperature range of 50.190 C.\"\n\n[8] \"One was that water enhances the water gas shift reaction and as a result more CO was converted into CO2, the second possibility was that the hydroxyl group formed on the catalyst upon adsorption of water was a better oxidation than oxygen and increases the oxidation rate of CO and hydrogen [18].\"\n\n[9] \"As compared to Pt/Al2O3 catalyst, the presence of water in the feed enhances the CO oxidation rate [6,22].\"", "English": "Bimetallic catalysts, particularly Pt-based ones like Pt-Pd, influence the mechanisms and efficiencies of CO oxidation through several means:\n\n1. Synergistic effects: The bimetallic system enhances catalyst properties through electronic and geometric effects, improving both activity and selectivity for CO oxidation.\n\n2. Particle dispersion and growth suppression: The superior activity of Pt-Pd catalysts is attributed to higher dispersion of supported particles and suppression of particle growth.\n\n3. Composition optimization: The catalytic activity increases with Pd content, with an optimal Pt:Pd ratio of 1:7 showing the best performance (76% CO conversion and 55% selectivity at 90-110°C).\n\n4. Oxygen concentration effects: Increasing O2 concentration improves CO conversion, with 99% conversion achieved at 2% O2 concentration.\n\n5. Water vapor enhancement: Adding 10% water vapor to the feed stream increases CO conversion from 76% to 85% at 90°C. This enhancement is attributed to two possible mechanisms:\n   a) Promotion of the water-gas shift reaction\n   b) Formation of hydroxyl groups on the catalyst surface, which are better oxidizers than oxygen\n\n6. {"Quotes": "[1] \"The formation of certain bimetallic clusters between Pt and Re or Pd and Re was confirmed in the cases of PtRe(2:3) and PdRe(1:1)/TiO2 catalysts; however a different addition manner was suggested for the later acceleration effect over PdRe(1:10)/TiO2 catalysts.\"\n\n[2] \"The activity of PdRe/TiO2 catalysts was strongly affected by the Re content, while the activity of PtRe/TiO2 catalysts was less dependent on the addition ratio of Re, and more dependent on the temperature of reduction.\"\n\n[3] \"The FT-IR analyses of the adsorbed species during the reaction exhibited the enhancement of the adsorbed CO peaks in lower wavenumber region with the increase of Re content. Accordingly, Re is supposed to have some effect on these adsorbed CO, which accelerates the WGS reaction, especially in the case of PdRe/TiO2 catalysts.\"\n\n[4] \"WGS reaction proceeds via the formation of the surface-formate anion over Re-added Pt and Pd catalysts, and the formation step of formats is the rate-determining step of WGS reaction.\"\n\n[5] \"The role of Re would be the stabilization of formate species and accelerate the rate of H2 formation.\"\n\n[6] \"PtRe/TiO2 system is known as a good catalyst showing activity close to Cu catalysts in low temperature\"\n\n[7] \"Under LTR condition, the change of the CO concentration only started at around 373 K; the most active catalysts was PtRe(2:0)/TiO2, and the addition of Re affected the reaction rate negatively.\"", "English": "Bimetallic catalysts, particularly Pt-based ones, influence the mechanisms and efficiencies of CO oxidation and water gas shift (WGS) reactions in several ways:\n\n1. Formation of bimetallic clusters: Pt-Re and Pd-Re bimetallic clusters form on TiO2 supports, affecting catalyst activity.\n\n2. Differential effects of Re content: \n   - PdRe/TiO2 catalysts are strongly influenced by Re content.\n   - PtRe/TiO2 catalysts are less affected by Re ratio but more by reduction temperature.\n   - PtRe/TiO2 shows good catalytic activity for WGS reactions at low temperatures, comparable to Cu catalysts.\n   - Under low temperature reduction (LTR) conditions, PtRe(2:0)/TiO2 was the most active catalyst, with Re addition negatively affecting the reaction rate.\n\n3. CO adsorption modification: \n   - Re addition enhances adsorbed CO peaks at lower wavenumbers.\n   - This suggests Re affects CO adsorption and accelerates the WGS reaction, especially for PdRe/TiO2 catalysts.\n\n4. Reaction mechanism: \n   - Re-added Pt and Pd catalysts promote WGS reaction through surface-formate anion formation.\n   - The formation of formate species is the rate-determining step of the WGS reaction.\n\n5. Stabilization of intermediates: Re appears to stabilize formate species on the catalyst surface, which helps accelerate the rate of H2 formation.\n\nFuture UHV studies could potentially provide insights by:\n1. Investigating the atomic-scale structure of bimetallic clusters on model surfaces.\n2. Examining the effects of different Re contents and reduction temperatures on surface properties.\n3. Studying CO adsorption behavior on well-defined bimetallic surfaces.\n4. Probing the formation and stability of surface intermediates like formate anions.\n\nThese UHV studies could help correlate reactor findings with model surfaces and supported catalysts by providing detailed information on surface structures, adsorption properties, and reaction intermediates under controlled conditions. Re含量的差异效应：\n   - PdRe/TiO2催化剂受Re含量的强烈影响。\n   - PtRe/TiO2催化剂受Re比例的影响较小，但更受还原温度的影响。\n   - PtRe/TiO2在低温下表现出良好的WGS反应催化活性，可与Cu催化剂相媲美。\n   - 在低温还原（LTR）条件下，PtRe(2:0)/TiO2是最活跃的催化剂，而Re的添加对反应速率产生了负面影响。\n\n3. CO吸附修饰：\n   - Re的添加增强了较低波数的吸附CO峰。\n   - 这表明Re影响CO吸附并加速WGS反应，尤其是对PdRe/TiO2催化剂。\n\n4. 反应机理：\n   - 添加Re的Pt和Pd催化剂通过表面甲酸根阴离子的形成促进WGS反应。\n   - 甲酸盐物种的形成是WGS反应的决速步骤。\n\n5. 稳定中间体：Re似乎能稳定催化剂表面的甲酸盐物种，这有助于加速H2的生成速率。\n\n未来的超高真空（UHV）研究可能通过以下方式提供见解：\n1. 研究模型表面上双金属簇的原子尺度结构。\n2. 检查不同Re含量和还原温度对表面性质的影响。\n3. 研究CO在定义明确的双金属表面上的吸附行为。\n4. 探测表面中间体（如甲酸根阴离子）的形成和稳定性。\n\n这些UHV研究可以通过在受控条件下提供表面结构、吸附性质和反应中间体的详细信息，帮助将反应器研究结果与模型表面和负载催化剂相关联。然而，当前UHV研究在Pt基双金属表面上的限制可能包括创建和表征复杂双金属结构的挑战，以及bridging UHV和反应器条件之间的压力差异。", "Doi": "10.1016/j.apcata.2005.08.009"},
{"Quotes": "[1] \"Our recent studies [21], [22] evidenced ruthenium as a good catalyst for CPO, though its stability needs to be improved and wide hysteresis cycles are observed while varying reaction temperature, apparently connected to the ease with which Ru is reduced and oxidized.\"\n\n[2] \"Conversely, Pt hardly undergoes redox reactions and it has some activity for CPO as well [23], [25]. In this work we present results of combining Pt and Ru on a bimetallic catalyst that showed good activity and selectivity towards CPO products and a much better stability than monometallic Ru.\"\n\n[3] \"The behavior of the bimetallic catalyst is similar to that of monometallic Pt at low T's, approaching monometallic Ru as the temperature rises. Interestingly, this feature implies that suitable proportions of Pt and Ru can determine the CO/H2 ratio at a given T.\"\n\n[4] \"Summarizing, we can conclude that Pt improves the stability of the catalyst preventing or limiting the Ru redox behavior. Conversely, a lower GHSV is required to achieve higher CO/H2 yields.\"\n\n[5] \"We developed a more efficient and stable catalyst for syngas production from methane. We combined the best features of Pt that activates methane at low temperature and those of Ru that is very selective towards CPO products.\"\n\n[6] \"Pt stabilizes Ru, limiting redox reactions during the heating and cooling cycles. The small residual hysteresis is likely caused by thermal effects and not by chemistry (reduction/oxidation reactions). The light-off temperature is also lower than for monometallic ruthenium, but the catalyst starts converting reactants following mainly total oxidation stoichiometry.\"\n\n[7] \"As temperature increases, CPO products clearly prevail and their ratio stabilizes at a value suitable for Fisher–Tropsch applications (H2/CO2 = 2). Even if not tested for many tens of hours, the catalyst did not show any marked aging effects, keeping its activity almost unchanged.\"", "English": "The Pt-Ru bimetallic catalyst influences the mechanisms and efficiencies of methane conversion in several ways:\n\n1. Improved stability: Pt stabilizes Ru by limiting redox reactions during temperature cycles, reducing hysteresis and improving overall stability compared to monometallic Ru catalysts.\n\n2. Lower light-off temperature: The bimetallic catalyst activates methane conversion at a lower temperature than monometallic Ru, though initially following total oxidation stoichiometry.\n\n3. Temperature-dependent behavior: At low temperatures, the catalyst behaves similarly to monometallic Pt, while at higher temperatures, it approaches the behavior of monometallic Ru.\n\n4. Reaction pathway: As temperature increases, partial oxidation products (CO and H2) become dominant, reaching a ratio suitable for Fischer-Tropsch applications (H2/CO = 2).\n\n5. Tunable product ratio: The CO/H2 ratio can be adjusted by changing the proportions of Pt and Ru in the catalyst.\n\n6. Reduced aging effects: The bimetallic catalyst shows minimal aging effects, maintaining its activity over time.\n\n7. Synergistic effects: The catalyst combines Pt's ability to activate methane at low temperatures with Ru's high selectivity towards CPO products.\n\n8. Trade-off in space velocity: Lower gas hourly space velocity (GHSV) is required to achieve higher CO/H2 yields compared to monometallic catalysts.\n\nThe literature does not specifically address CO oxidation or water gas shift reactions for this catalyst system. Future UHV studies on Pt-based bimetallic surfaces could potentially provide atomic-level insights into:\n\n1. The synergistic effects between Pt and Ru in methane activation and product selectivity.\n2. The mechanisms behind Pt's stabilizing effect on Ru.\n3. The transition from total oxidation to partial oxidation as temperature increases.\n4. The role of each metal in various reaction steps.\n\nSuch studies could help correlate reactor findings with model surfaces and supported catalysts, bridging the gap between applied catalysis and fundamental surface science. However, it's important to note that UHV studies on Pt-based bimetallic surfaces have limitations in directly correlating to supported catalysts under reaction conditions. Bridging this \"pressure gap\" remains a challenge in catalysis research.", "Chinese": "Pt-Ru双金属催化剂以几种方式影响甲烷转化的机理和效率：\n\n1. 改善稳定性：Pt通过限制温度循环过程中的氧化还原反应来稳定Ru，减少滞后现象，与单金属Ru催化剂相比，整体稳定性得到改善。\n\n2. 更低的点火温度：双金属催化剂在比单金属Ru更低的温度下激活甲烷转化，尽管最初遵循完全氧化化学计量比。\n\n3. 温度依赖性行为：在低温下，催化剂的行为类似于单金属Pt，而在高温下，其行为接近单金属Ru。\n\n4. 反应途径：随着温度升高，部分氧化产物（CO和H2）变得占主导地位，达到适合费-托合成的比例（H2/CO = 2）。\n\n5. 可调节的产物比例：通过改变催化剂中Pt和Ru的比例，可以调节CO/H2比率。\n\n6. 老化效应减少：双金属催化剂显示出最小的老化效应，随时间保持其活性。\n\n7. 协同效应：催化剂结合了Pt在低温下激活甲烷的能力和Ru对CPO产物的高选择性。\n\n8. 空速权衡：与单金属催化剂相比，需要较低的气体小时空速（GHSV）来获得更高的CO/H2产率。\n\n文献没有具体讨论该催化剂系统的CO氧化或水气变换反应。未来对Pt基双金属表面的超高真空（UHV）研究可能会提供原子级别的洞见：\n\n1. {"Quotes": "[1] \"The PtSnOx system has been studied for many years as it has shown to catalyze the CO oxidation at moderate temperatures (ca. 120 C), where neither platinum nor tin dioxide alone has stable activity. {"Quotes": "[1] \"Among the reported heterogeneous catalysts so far for the CO oxidation, PROX reaction and cathodic materials of the PEM fuel cells, supported Pt-Fe nanoparticles prepared by one improved method have been investigated by several groups\"\n\n[2] \"They proposed a so-called bifunctional mechanism and pointed out that the mechanism was clearly different to that of the PROX reaction on Au catalysts supported on TiO2, Al2O3 and ZrO2\"\n\n[3] \"Up to know, a noncompetitive dual site mechanism has been proposed for the PROX reaction over the supported bimetallic Pt-Fe catalyst\"\n\n[4] \"It means that platinum site in Pto state acts as CO adsorption site and iron site in FeOx or Feo state as an O2 dissociative-adsorption site enhances the surface reaction between the reactants on the neighboring sites.\"\n\n[5] \"Very recently, Siani et al. reported the silica-supported Pt, PtFe2 and Pt5Fe2 catalysts prepared from PtFe2(COD)(CO)8 (COD = 1,5-cyclooctadiene) and Pt5Fe2(COD)2(CO)12 organometallic cluster precursors, respectively\"\n\n[6] \"The cluster-derived PtFe/SiO2 catalyst showed improved CO oxidation activity in the presence and absence of hydrogen as compared to that prepared by the conventional methods.\"", "English": "Bimetallic Pt-based catalysts, particularly Pt-Fe systems, significantly influence CO oxidation and related reactions through several mechanisms:\n\n1. Bifunctional mechanism: In Pt-Fe catalysts, Pt sites act as CO adsorption sites while Fe sites serve as O2 dissociative-adsorption sites. This synergistic effect enhances surface reactions between reactants on neighboring sites.\n\n2. Noncompetitive dual site mechanism: This has been proposed for the preferential oxidation (PROX) reaction over supported bimetallic Pt-Fe catalysts.\n\n3. Improved activity: Pt-Fe catalysts, especially those derived from organometallic cluster precursors, have shown enhanced CO oxidation activity compared to conventionally prepared catalysts, both in the presence and absence of hydrogen.\n\n4. {"Quotes": "[1] \"Pt-based intermetallic compounds (IMCs) supported on silica were studied as a catalyst for the preferential oxidation (PROX) of CO in excess hydrogen to obtain the active catalyst at low temperatures.\"\n\n[2] \"Pt3Co/SiO2 and PtCu/SiO2 were more active than Pt/SiO2 and Pt/Al2O3 in the temperature range of 373453 K.\"\n\n[3] \"Infrared (IR), X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS), and adsorption measurements revealed a significant electron transfer from Pt atoms to Co or Cu atoms. The electron-deficient Pt atoms adsorbed CO weakly compared with Pt metal, accelerating the adsorption of oxygen on the IMC surface.\"\n\n[4] \"Kinetic studies indicated that Co and Cu atoms in IMCs also adsorb oxygen. This improved oxygen adsorption likely resulted in the high PROX activity at low temperatures.\"\n\n[5] \"The reaction proceeded through the LangmuirHinshelwood mechanism, as has been proposed on PtFe/mordenite\"\n\n[6] \"On PtCu/SiO2, however, CO conversion increased by 30% with the addition of hydrogen and even further by the addition of water. The enhancing effect of hydrogen reflected the contribution of water produced by the oxidation of hydrogen during the PROX reaction.\"\n\n[7] \"The CO molecules on Pt would be oxidized by oxygen atoms activated on Co, resulting in higher activity of Pt3Co compared with Pt metal.\"", "English": "Pt-based bimetallic catalysts, particularly intermetallic compounds (IMCs) like Pt3Co and PtCu, significantly influence CO oxidation mechanisms and efficiencies in reactor studies. These catalysts show higher activity than pure Pt catalysts at lower temperatures (373-453 K) for preferential oxidation (PROX) of CO in excess hydrogen.\n\nThe enhanced performance of these bimetallic catalysts is attributed to several factors:\n\n1. Electronic effects: Electron transfer from Pt to Co or Cu atoms results in electron-deficient Pt atoms that adsorb CO more weakly than pure Pt, facilitating oxygen adsorption.\n\n2. Improved oxygen adsorption: Co and Cu atoms in the IMCs also adsorb oxygen, contributing to higher PROX activity at low temperatures.\n\n3. Reaction mechanism: The reaction proceeds through a Langmuir-Hinshelwood mechanism, differing from the Rideal mechanism observed on pure Pt surfaces.\n\n4. Synergistic effects: On Pt3Co, CO adsorbed on Pt is oxidized by oxygen atoms activated on Co sites, resulting in higher activity compared to pure Pt.\n\n5. Hydrogen and water effects: For PtCu catalysts, the presence of hydrogen and water significantly enhances CO conversion. The addition of hydrogen increases CO conversion by 30%, with further enhancement by water addition. This effect is attributed to the water produced during the PROX reaction.\n\nThe study does not provide direct information on water gas shift reactions or methane conversions for these bimetallic catalysts. \n\nFuture UHV studies could potentially provide valuable insights by:\n\n1. Investigating the surface structure and composition of well-defined bimetallic surfaces under reaction conditions.\n2. Studying the adsorption and reaction of CO, oxygen, and hydrogen on these surfaces at a molecular level.\n3. Examining the effects of water on the surface chemistry of these bimetallic catalysts.\n4. Comparing the reactivity of model surfaces with supported catalysts to understand the role of the support and particle size effects.\n\nSuch UHV studies could bridge the gap between reactor studies and model surfaces, providing atomic-level insights into the mechanisms underlying the enhanced performance of bimetallic catalysts. This could potentially lead to the design of more efficient catalysts for CO oxidation and related reactions.", "Chinese": "基于铂的双金属催化剂，特别是Pt3Co和PtCu等金属间化合物（IMCs），在反应器研究中显著影响CO氧化机理和效率。这些催化剂在较低温度下（373-453 K）对过量氢气中CO的优先氧化（PROX）表现出比纯Pt催化剂更高的活性。\n\n这些双金属催化剂的增强性能归因于几个因素：\n\n1. 电子效应：Pt向Co或Cu原子的电子转移导致Pt原子缺电子，与纯Pt相比更弱地吸附CO，从而促进氧气吸附。\n\n2. 改善的氧气吸附：IMCs中的Co和Cu原子也吸附氧气，有助于在低温下提高PROX活性。\n\n3. 反应机理：反应通过Langmuir-Hinshelwood机理进行，与纯Pt表面上观察到的Rideal机理不同。\n\n4. 协同效应：在Pt3Co上，吸附在Pt上的CO被在Co位点上活化的氧原子氧化，导致比纯Pt更高的活性。\n\n5. 氢气和水的效应：对于PtCu催化剂，氢气和水的存在显著增强了CO转化。添加氢气使CO转化率增加30%，添加水进一步增强了这一效果。这种效应归因于PROX反应过程中产生的水。\n\n该研究没有直接提供这些双金属催化剂在水煤气变换反应或甲烷转化方面的信息。\n\n未来的超高真空（UHV）研究可能通过以下方式提供有价值的见解：\n\n1. 研究反应条件下定义明确的双金属表面的表面结构和组成。\n2. 在分子水平上研究CO、氧气和氢气在这些表面上的吸附和反应。\n3. 检查水对这些双金属催化剂表面化学的影响。\n4. 比较模型表面与负载型催化剂的反应活性，以了解载体和粒子尺寸效应的作用。\n\n这些UHV研究可以弥合反应器研究与模型表面之间的差距，提供对双金属催化剂增强性能背后机理的原子水平见解。这可能导致设计出更高效的CO氧化和相关反应的催化剂。", "Doi": "10.1016/j.jcat.2008.06.030"},
{"Quotes": "[1] \"Modification of Pt/SiO2 with ReOx species enhanced the catalytic activity of the CO oxidation with O2 in the presence of H2.\"\n\n          [2] \"The promoting effect of Re species appeared after the reduction above 673 K.\"\n\n          [3] \"The reduced PtReOx/SiO2 (Re/Pt = 0.5) has high O2 activation ability even when the CO adsorption on the Pt surface atoms is saturated, and this property is caused by the reduced Re species.\"\n\n          [4] \"Under the PROX condition, the reduced state of Re species can be maintained by the presence of H2. {"Quotes": "\"Among them AuPt/CeO2 catalyst shows the highest activity with 78% conversion of CO at 250 C.\"\n\n\"The activity increases obviously with Pt loadings in AuPt/CeO2. {"Quotes": "\"The key for the improvement of the CO oxidation rate is to allow for a non-competitive dual-site mechanism for CO and O2. New catalyst formulations are being developed towards supplying these catalysts with an additional site for oxygen adsorption, which will enhance the reaction rate, by addition of a promoter\"\n\n\"An example of this development is the addition of Fe as a promoter for Pt catalysts. The Pt serves as the site for CO adsorption, whereas the Fe oxide promoter dissociates the O2 molecule, resulting in a non-competitive, dual-site mechanism.\"\n\n\"MnOx is reported as high oxygen storage capacity compound. MnOx has been studied in oxidation reactions and as support for Au catalyst in the PROX reaction. MnOx-doped Pt catalysts have been studied for automotive pollution control and for CO oxidation (in H2-free streams).\"\n\n\"Comparing the PROX behavior of all catalysts in Fig. 5(a), we can see that those with a higher content in MnOx (P1M8ASI and P1M15ASI) are more active than Pt/Al2O3, with the following order of activity: P1M15ASI > P1M8ASI > P1A > P1M2ASI > M2P1ASI ≈ P1M2ACI ≈ M2A.\"\n\n\"While the WGS reaction is beneficial in its forward direction, methanation reactions are always detrimental and should be avoided.\"", "English": "Bimetallic catalysts, particularly Pt-based ones, significantly influence CO oxidation mechanisms and efficiencies through a non-competitive dual-site mechanism. {"Quotes": "[1] \"The addition of Re to Pt/Ce0.46Zr0.54O2 was shown to enhance the watergas shift (WGS) rate compared with the rate observed with Pt alone supported on either Ce0.46Zr0.54O2 or Ce0.6Zr0.4O2 at similar Pt weight loadings.\"\n\n[2] \"The results from CO chemisorption showed that the Pt was more highly dispersed on Pt-Re/Ce0.46Zr0.54O2 than on the Pt/Ce0.46Zr0.54O2 or Pt/Ce0.6Zr0.4O2.\"\n\n[3] \"The WGS rate was observed to be proportional to the exposed Pt surface area for the Pt-Re and Pt catalysts; however, the rate per m2 of exposed Pt for Pt-Re/ Ce0.46Zr0.54O2 was higher than that of Pt/Ce0.46Zr0.54O2 or Pt/Ce0.6Zr0.4O2.\"\n\n[4] \"The difference in the rates upon the addition of Re to Pt WGS catalysts suggests that the role of Re in enhancing the WGS activity of Pt is more complex than to just increase the Pt dispersion.\"\n\n[5] \"If the only function of Re was to increase the Pt dispersion, one would expect the same WGS activity for both Pt and Pt-Re catalysts.\"\n\n[6] \"A bifunctional redox mechanism is used to explain this synergism. In this mechanism, CO is adsorbed on the platinum, then oxygen is transferred from the ceria to the platinum, where the CO is oxidized (CO2) and the ceria is reduced (Ce4+  Ce3+); finally, the reduced ceria is reoxidized (Ce3+  Ce4+) by the dissociative adsorption of H2O, releasing H2 in the process.\"", "English": "Bimetallic catalysts, particularly Pt-based ones like Pt-Re, significantly influence the mechanisms and efficiencies of the water gas shift (WGS) reaction in reactor studies. The addition of Re to Pt/Ce0.46Zr0.54O2 enhances the WGS rate compared to Pt alone on similar supports. This enhancement is partly due to increased Pt dispersion, as shown by CO chemisorption studies. However, the effect goes beyond just improved dispersion, as the rate per unit of exposed Pt surface area is higher for Pt-Re catalysts than for Pt alone.\n\nThe mechanism for the WGS reaction on these catalysts is believed to be a bifunctional redox mechanism, where CO adsorbs on Pt, oxygen transfers from the ceria support to Pt for CO oxidation, and the reduced ceria is then reoxidized by water, releasing hydrogen.\n\nThe synergistic effect between Pt and Re suggests possible electronic or structural modifications that affect the catalytic properties. The role of Re in enhancing the WGS activity of Pt is more complex than simply increasing Pt dispersion.\n\nCurrent reactor studies provide valuable insights into the performance of these bimetallic catalysts, but they have limitations in elucidating the precise nature of the active sites and reaction mechanisms at the atomic scale. Future UHV studies on model Pt-based bimetallic surfaces could potentially bridge this gap by allowing detailed investigation of surface structures, adsorption properties, and reaction intermediates under well-controlled conditions.\n\nSuch UHV studies could help correlate the findings from reactor studies with atomic-scale phenomena on model surfaces and supported catalysts. They could provide insights into how the addition of Re modifies the electronic structure of Pt, affects the adsorption and activation of reactants, and influences the formation and stability of reaction intermediates. This information could be crucial for understanding the observed synergistic effects and for rational design of more efficient bimetallic catalysts.\n\nHowever, it's important to note that there are current limitations in UHV studies on Pt-based bimetallic surfaces, particularly in replicating the complex environment of supported catalysts under reaction conditions. Bridging the gap between UHV studies and real catalytic systems remains a significant challenge in the field.", "Chinese": "双金属催化剂，特别是基于铂的催化剂如铂-铼，在反应器研究中显著影响水气转化（WGS）反应的机理和效率。与单独的Pt催化剂相比，在相似支撑体上添加Re可以提高WGS反应速率。CO化学吸附研究表明，这种增强部分归因于Pt分散度的提高。然而，这种效果不仅仅是分散度改善，因为Pt-Re催化剂的单位暴露Pt表面积反应速率高于单独的Pt催化剂。\n\n这些催化剂上WGS反应的机理被认为是一种双功能氧化还原机制，其中CO吸附在铂上，氧从氧化铈载体转移到铂上进行CO氧化，然后还原的氧化铈被水重新氧化，释放出氢气。\n\nPt和Re之间的协同效应暗示可能存在影响催化性能的电子或结构修饰。Re在增强Pt的WGS活性中的作用比单纯增加Pt分散度更为复杂。\n\n当前的反应器研究为这些双金属催化剂的性能提供了宝贵的见解，但在阐明原子尺度上活性位点和反应机理的精确本质方面存在局限性。未来在模型Pt基双金属表面上进行的超高真空（UHV）研究可能会弥补这一差距，允许在严格控制的条件下详细研究表面结构、吸附性质和反应中间体。\n\n这些UHV研究可以帮助将反应器研究的发现与模型表面和负载催化剂上的原子尺度现象相关联。它们可以提供关于Re的添加如何修改Pt的电子结构、影响反应物的吸附和活化以及影响反应中间体的形成和稳定性的见解。这些信息对于理解观察到的协同效应和理性设计更高效的双金属催化剂至关重要。\n\n然而，值得注意的是，在Pt基双金属表面上进行UHV研究目前存在一些限制，特别是在复制反应条件下负载催化剂的复杂环境方面。在UHV研究和实际催化系统之间架起桥梁仍然是该领域的一个重大挑战。", "Doi": "10.1016/j.cattod.2004.10.002"},

{"Quotes": "[1] \"The catalyst is 0.5% Ru and 0.5% Pt (w/w) supported on mixture of alumina, ceria and zirconia (75/4.4/20.6%, w/w), washcoated on a ceramic monolith.\"\n\n[2] \"We already studied the activity of this 0.5/0.5% Pt/Ru catalyst for partial oxidation, speculating that combustion and reforming of methane occurs sequentially, and that is clearly identified also by tests on the global reaction, without studying each single reaction in the mechanism.\"\n\n[3] \"Through specific tests with selected mixtures, we proved that the PtRu catalyst supports the indirect combustion and reforming mechanism in CPO, as already suggested in a previous work.\"\n\n[4] \"The catalyst was active in catalysing all the candidate reactions (steam reforming, dry reforming and direct/reverse water-gas shift).\"\n\n[5] \"Both the direct and the reverse water-gas shift reactions are very fast and not affected by the gas space velocity. It supports an indirect combustion and reforming mechanism for catalytic partial oxidation (CPO) of methane, where complete combustion occurs first, followed by reforming reactions.\n\n2. Different supports are optimal for different temperature ranges:\n   - PdPtAl2O3 was most active in the low-temperature region\n   - PdPt on ceria-stabilized ZrO2 was most active between 620 and 800°C\n   - PdPt on LaMnAl11O19 was superior above 800°C\n\n5. There is evidence of close interaction between Pd and Pt in the bimetallic catalysts, which likely contributes to their improved performance.\n\n6. The bimetallic catalysts typically had a molar ratio of 2:1 Pd:Pt.\n\n7. The activity of PdPt catalysts increased over time, likely due to PdO formation during operation.\n\n8. ZrO2-based supports helped suppress the drop in methane conversion during PdO decomposition compared to Al2O3 supports.\n\n9. {"Quotes": "[1] \"Among a number of catalysts reported to be active for PROX, supported platinum catalysts have been considered to be promising in view of their high catalytic performance.\"\n\n[2] \"PtCo bimetallic catalyst supported on yttria-stabilized zirconia (YSZ) is highly efficient for PROX in a H2-rich gas stream even with a small amount of Pt (0.5wt%) at temperatures below 423K.\"\n\n[3] \"The presence of isolated bimetallic PtCo nanoparticles interacting with the support seems to give rise to this high catalytic activity.\"\n\n[4] \"For CO oxidation, it has been proposed that the lattice oxygen and interfacial metalsupport interaction play a crucial role in promoting CO oxidation when metal species are supported on an oxygen-ion-conducting support.\"\n\n[5] \"Temperature-programmed reduction (TPR) was conducted to try to determine the interactions between Pt and Co, as well as those between Pt, Co oxides (CoOx), and YSZ\"\n\n[6] \"Three main reactions take place in this system. The reaction that competes most effectively with CO oxidation [Eq.(1)] is H2 oxidation [Eq.(2)] because of the H2-rich conditions in the gas stream in practical fuel cell applications. In addition, CO can consume additional H2 by undergoing hydrogenation [Eq.(3)], a process also known as methanation, which should be avoided unless the CO concentration in the reactant stream is quite low, because it consumes relatively large amounts of hydrogen (3mol per mol CO).\"", "English": "Bimetallic catalysts, particularly Pt-based ones like PtCo, significantly influence the mechanisms and efficiencies of CO oxidation, water gas shift reaction, and methane conversions in reactor studies. PtCo bimetallic catalysts supported on yttria-stabilized zirconia (YSZ) demonstrate high efficiency for preferential CO oxidation (PROX) in hydrogen-rich streams, even with low Pt content (0.5wt%) at temperatures below 423K.\n\nThe enhanced catalytic activity is attributed to the presence of isolated bimetallic PtCo nanoparticles interacting with the support. For CO oxidation, lattice oxygen and interfacial metal-support interactions play crucial roles when metal species are supported on oxygen-ion-conducting supports like YSZ.\n\nThe study used temperature-programmed reduction (TPR) to investigate the interactions between Pt, Co, and the YSZ support, providing insights into the formation and behavior of the bimetallic phase. This technique revealed the presence of new bimetallic PtCo oxides and their reduction at lower temperatures compared to monometallic catalysts.\n\nIn the catalytic system, three main reactions occur: CO oxidation, H2 oxidation, and CO hydrogenation (methanation). H2 oxidation competes most effectively with CO oxidation due to H2-rich conditions in practical fuel cell applications. Methanation should be avoided unless CO concentration is low, as it consumes large amounts of hydrogen.\n\nWhile this research provides valuable insights from reactor studies, it does not directly address UHV studies on Pt-based bimetallic surfaces. Future UHV studies could potentially offer more detailed information on atomic-scale interactions and surface chemistry, helping to correlate findings from reactor studies with model surfaces and supported catalysts. However, UHV studies face limitations in replicating complex catalytic environments, particularly in terms of pressure and the presence of support materials. Bridging the gap between UHV studies and real catalytic conditions remains a challenge in correlating findings with model surfaces and supported catalysts.", "Chinese": "双金属催化剂，特别是以Pt为基础的催化剂（如PtCo），在反应器研究中显著影响了CO氧化、水煤气变换反应和甲烷转化的机理和效率。以氧化钇稳定的氧化锆（YSZ）为载体的PtCo双金属催化剂在富氢气流中对优先CO氧化（PROX）表现出高效性，即使在低Pt含量（0.5wt%）和423K以下的温度下也是如此。\n\n增强的催化活性归因于与载体相互作用的孤立双金属PtCo纳米粒子的存在。对于CO氧化，当金属物种被负载在氧离子导电载体（如YSZ）上时，晶格氧和金属-载体界面相互作用起着至关重要的作用。\n\n研究使用温度程序还原（TPR）技术来研究Pt、Co和YSZ载体之间的相互作用，从而深入了解双金属相的形成和行为。这种技术揭示了新的双金属PtCo氧化物的存在，以及它们相比单金属催化剂在更低温度下的还原过程。\n\n在催化系统中，主要发生三种反应：CO氧化、H2氧化和CO加氢（甲烷化）。由于实际燃料电池应用中富氢条件的存在，H2氧化最有效地与CO氧化竞争。除非CO浓度较低，否则应避免甲烷化，因为它消耗大量氢气。\n\n虽然这项研究提供了反应器研究的宝贵见解，但它并未直接涉及Pt基双金属表面的超高真空（UHV）研究。未来的UHV研究可能会提供原子尺度相互作用和表面化学的更详细信息，有助于将反应器研究的发现与模型表面和负载催化剂相关联。然而，UHV研究在复制复杂的催化环境方面面临局限性，特别是在压力和载体材料存在的方面。弥合UHV研究与实际催化条件之间的差距仍然是将研究结果与模型表面和负载催化剂相关联的一个挑战。", "Doi": "10.1002/anie.200603144"},

{"Quotes": "[1] \"Many studies have been made on the approach of combinatorial catalysis especially Pt and Pd for CO oxidation reaction [10]. At 90 C, when there was no water vapor in the feed stream the CO conversion was about 76% and when adding 10% water vapor in the feed stream the CO conversion was increased to 85%.\"\n\n[7] \"The CO conversion substantially dropped from 76% to 50% at 90.110 C when increasing CO2 concentration in the feed stream. Particle dispersion and growth suppression: The superior activity of Pt-Pd catalysts is attributed to higher dispersion of supported particles and suppression of particle growth.\n\n3. Composition optimization: The catalytic activity increases with Pd content, with an optimal Pt:Pd ratio of 1:7 showing the best performance (76% CO conversion and 55% selectivity at 90-110°C).\n\n4. Oxygen concentration effects: Increasing O2 concentration improves CO conversion, with 99% conversion achieved at 2% O2 concentration.\n\n5. CO吸附修饰：\n   - Re的添加增强了较低波数的吸附CO峰。\n   - 这表明Re影响CO吸附并加速WGS反应，尤其是对PdRe/TiO2催化剂。\n\n4. 反应机理：\n   - 添加Re的Pt和Pd催化剂通过表面甲酸根阴离子的形成促进WGS反应。\n   - 甲酸盐物种的形成是WGS反应的决速步骤。\n\n5. 稳定中间体：Re似乎能稳定催化剂表面的甲酸盐物种，这有助于加速H2的生成速率。\n\n未来的超高真空（UHV）研究可能通过以下方式提供见解：\n1. 研究模型表面上双金属簇的原子尺度结构。\n2. 检查不同Re含量和还原温度对表面性质的影响。\n3. 研究CO在定义明确的双金属表面上的吸附行为。\n4. 探测表面中间体（如甲酸根阴离子）的形成和稳定性。\n\n这些UHV研究可以通过在受控条件下提供表面结构、吸附性质和反应中间体的详细信息，帮助将反应器研究结果与模型表面和负载催化剂相关联。然而，当前UHV研究在Pt基双金属表面上的限制可能包括创建和表征复杂双金属结构的挑战，以及bridging UHV和反应器条件之间的压力差异。", "Doi": "10.1016/j.apcata.2005.08.009"},
{"Quotes": "[1] \"Our recent studies [21], [22] evidenced ruthenium as a good catalyst for CPO, though its stability needs to be improved and wide hysteresis cycles are observed while varying reaction temperature, apparently connected to the ease with which Ru is reduced and oxidized.\"\n\n[2] \"Conversely, Pt hardly undergoes redox reactions and it has some activity for CPO as well [23], [25]. In this work we present results of combining Pt and Ru on a bimetallic catalyst that showed good activity and selectivity towards CPO products and a much better stability than monometallic Ru.\"\n\n[3] \"The behavior of the bimetallic catalyst is similar to that of monometallic Pt at low T's, approaching monometallic Ru as the temperature rises. Interestingly, this feature implies that suitable proportions of Pt and Ru can determine the CO/H2 ratio at a given T.\"\n\n[4] \"Summarizing, we can conclude that Pt improves the stability of the catalyst preventing or limiting the Ru redox behavior. Conversely, a lower GHSV is required to achieve higher CO/H2 yields.\"\n\n[5] \"We developed a more efficient and stable catalyst for syngas production from methane. We combined the best features of Pt that activates methane at low temperature and those of Ru that is very selective towards CPO products.\"\n\n[6] \"Pt stabilizes Ru, limiting redox reactions during the heating and cooling cycles. The small residual hysteresis is likely caused by thermal effects and not by chemistry (reduction/oxidation reactions). The light-off temperature is also lower than for monometallic ruthenium, but the catalyst starts converting reactants following mainly total oxidation stoichiometry.\"\n\n[7] \"As temperature increases, CPO products clearly prevail and their ratio stabilizes at a value suitable for Fisher–Tropsch applications (H2/CO2 = 2). Even if not tested for many tens of hours, the catalyst did not show any marked aging effects, keeping its activity almost unchanged.\"", "English": "The Pt-Ru bimetallic catalyst influences the mechanisms and efficiencies of methane conversion in several ways:\n\n1. Improved stability: Pt stabilizes Ru by limiting redox reactions during temperature cycles, reducing hysteresis and improving overall stability compared to monometallic Ru catalysts.\n\n2. Lower light-off temperature: The bimetallic catalyst activates methane conversion at a lower temperature than monometallic Ru, though initially following total oxidation stoichiometry.\n\n3. Temperature-dependent behavior: At low temperatures, the catalyst behaves similarly to monometallic Pt, while at higher temperatures, it approaches the behavior of monometallic Ru.\n\n4. Reaction pathway: As temperature increases, partial oxidation products (CO and H2) become dominant, reaching a ratio suitable for Fischer-Tropsch applications (H2/CO = 2).\n\n5. Tunable product ratio: The CO/H2 ratio can be adjusted by changing the proportions of Pt and Ru in the catalyst.\n\n6. Reduced aging effects: The bimetallic catalyst shows minimal aging effects, maintaining its activity over time.\n\n7. Synergistic effects: The catalyst combines Pt's ability to activate methane at low temperatures with Ru's high selectivity towards CPO products.\n\n8. Trade-off in space velocity: Lower gas hourly space velocity (GHSV) is required to achieve higher CO/H2 yields compared to monometallic catalysts.\n\nThe literature does not specifically address CO oxidation or water gas shift reactions for this catalyst system. Future UHV studies on Pt-based bimetallic surfaces could potentially provide atomic-level insights into:\n\n1. The synergistic effects between Pt and Ru in methane activation and product selectivity.\n2. The mechanisms behind Pt's stabilizing effect on Ru.\n3. The transition from total oxidation to partial oxidation as temperature increases.\n4. The role of each metal in various reaction steps.\n\nSuch studies could help correlate reactor findings with model surfaces and supported catalysts, bridging the gap between applied catalysis and fundamental surface science. However, it's important to note that UHV studies on Pt-based bimetallic surfaces have limitations in directly correlating to supported catalysts under reaction conditions. {"Quotes": "[1] \"The co-impregnated PtNi/γ-Al2O3 was superior to Pt/Ni/γ-Al2O3 and Ni/Pt/γ-Al2O3 prepared by a sequential impregnation of each component on alumina support.\"\n\n          [2] \"As the reduction temperature increased above 423 K, the CO2 selectivity decreased and the atomic percent of Ni in the bimetallic phase of PtNi increased.\"\n\n          [3] \"This catalyst exhibited the high CO conversion even in the presence of 2% H2O and 20% CO2 over a wide reaction temperature.\"\n\n          [4] \"The bimetallic phase of PtNi seems to give rise to high catalytic activity for the PROX in H2-rich stream.\"", "English": "The literature provides insights into how Pt-based bimetallic catalysts, specifically PtNi, influence CO oxidation mechanisms and efficiencies. The bimetallic phase of PtNi was found to be crucial for high catalytic activity in PROX reactions.\n\n          The reduction temperature significantly affects catalyst performance. Higher reduction temperatures above 423 K led to decreased CO2 selectivity but increased the atomic percent of Ni in the bimetallic PtNi phase. The catalyst maintained high CO conversion even in the presence of water and CO2, indicating its effectiveness in realistic reaction conditions.\n\n          While the study focuses on CO oxidation, it doesn't directly address water gas shift reactions or methane conversions.
